  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_776b45c4-1e3c-47a1-aec1-1220cea3c334'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

He is starting over: new city, new friends, and new profession.<br /><br />But when he learns that Logan might actually be alive and in hiding, Kylar is faced with an agonizing choice: will he give up the way of shadows forever and live in peace with his new family, or will he risk everything by taking on the ultimate hit?<br /><br />Devour this blockbuster tale of assassination and magic by Brent Weeks, which has delighted readers all over the world--with over one million copies in print!</span>

<div id="review_280034592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280034592" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280034592?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I wouldn't recommend it.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280034592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12358955747305281843"><br/>My ocular muscles are sore from all the eyerolling I did when I read <i>Shadow's Edge</i>. <b>It is even more obsessed with virginity/chastity than an average American Sex Ed class.</b> Because all women are either virgins or whores, right? <i>*sigh*</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723009.jpg' width='400' height='240' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The terrible, atrocious portrayal of female characters annoyed me even more than in the first book. <b>
  <i>I cringed very time a female character took stage.</i>
</b> They all lack any depth whatsoever, becoming little more than caricatures. <b>The virgin/whore dichotomy </b>rules thi</span>
  <span id="freeText12358955747305281843" style="display:none"><br>My ocular muscles are sore from all the eyerolling I did when I read <i>Shadow's Edge</i>. <b>It is even more obsessed with virginity/chastity than an average American Sex Ed class.</b> Because all women are either virgins or whores, right? <i>*sigh*</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723009.jpg" width="400" height="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The terrible, atrocious portrayal of female characters annoyed me even more than in the first book. <b>
  <i>I cringed very time a female character took stage.</i>
</b> They all lack any depth whatsoever, becoming little more than caricatures. <b>The virgin/whore dichotomy </b>rules this book and the entire worth of a woman is reduced to her sexuality. This may be the view of this quasi-medieval society, but we are not shown anything to disprove it at all. This is NOT.COOL. <blockquote> Sidenote: <i>By the way, can somebody please explain to me why EVERY SINGLE "GOOD" CHARACTER (men included, at least no misogyny there) must be a virgin? Because CLEARLY the state of your reproductive organs is what determines who you are.</i> *cue exasperated eyeroll*</blockquote>The only acceptable state of unmarried genitalia.<br>.................<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723010.jpg" width="170" height="130" class="gr-hostedUserImg">...............<br>-------------------------------------------------------<br><b>Ladies and gentlemen, let me introduce you to some examples of the aforementioned virgin-whore situation we've got on our hands:</b><br><br>.....<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723011.jpg" width="300" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg">......<br><br><b>EXHIBIT A: ELENE (VIRGIN):</b> Saintly mind-numbingly boring Elene is clearly the embodiment of goodness in this book (and the entire story arc, as the events of the sequel show). She is supposed to be sweet, kind, and innocent. She tries to help Kylar denounce his former murdering ways by turning him into a mundane law-abiding peacefully-living sorta-spouse. <br><br>Well, that's good, right? Well, unless you take the only guy that can use his super-powers to save thousands of the inhabitants of his hometown from bloodthirsty invaders and force him to leave he city and start a 'regular' life with you - as long as he does not kill, even the bad guys. Let me repeat - <b>
  <i>she abhors murder and thus removes from the city the only guy WHO COULD HAVE STOPPED THOUSANDS FROM BEING MURDERED.</i>
</b> Instead of righting the wrongs, Kylar gets to be all sickeningly cute and sugary with Elene while attempting to raise the world's most annoying child ever. <br><br><i>
  <b>Both my hand and my head hurt from the endless facepalming in addition to all the eyerolling.</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723012.jpg" width="170" height="130" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> and <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723013.jpg" width="170" height="130" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><p><b>EXHIBIT B: VI (WHORE):</b> Unlike whiny Elene, Vi is a trained assassin. She is supposed to be a badass, but a deeply flawed one. Well, apparently all her badassery goes out the window the moment Kylar's sexy man-charms reach her. And ALL of her problems obviously stem from being sexually used from a young age. <b>But hey, there's still hope for her since all those bad sexy things she's done - yeah, none of those were for pleasure, so it's gotta be okay.</b><br>----------------------------------------------------------<br>The rest of the characters remain rather flat and underdeveloped in this exclusively plot-driven story. We are quickly introduced to a slew of characters, given one or two defining characteristics, and move on. And these characteristics are told, not shown. <b>In the whirlwind switch between POVs every few pages, we lose what little character development there could have been, since no page time is devoted to showing any of it.</b> <br><br>For instance, I know that Kylar and Logan are supposed to be best friends, to the point where Kylar is willing to risk everything for Logan's sake. I know Kylar and Jarl are supposed to be like brothers. I know Kylar is supposed to be madly in love with Elene. Unfortunately I only know that because I was told that at some point, often by the characters themselves, but I have not seen any interaction between any of them in the book to actually convince me and show me that those feelings and emotions are true. <b>With all the telling but little showing, I just don't believe the characters' motivations; their actions just become the ways to advance the plot and not much more. </b><br>--------------------------------------------------------<br><br>Despite all of my issues with this book, this was still a better story than the first installment. The action scenes remain fun and well-written. The plot, after the stumbling block of Elene-Kylar tortured love, picks up and moves at a breakneck speed. The loose ends continue to be nicely tied up, even if often in a predictable way. <b>Basically, this can be a quick, fun and mindless read, if you don't stop and think much along the way. </b>I still think that Weeks has potential if he learns better characterization; his storytelling skills are already better than many fantasy writers. <b><s>3 stars</s> 2 stars¹.</b> </p><blockquote>¹ After realizing that I have given 3 stars to quite a few books that I liked way more than this one (and its predecessor), I realized that the fair thing to do would be to knock this one down a star. For the life of me, I have no idea why I was so generous with rating it in the first place.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12358955747305281843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer631994067673868776">Some time has passed, and I’m trying to think of something positive to say about this book. And it turns out to be a real struggle.<br/><br/>Most of it is about Kylar constantly complaining that he’s a virgin, Logan constantly complaining that he’s a virgin, Elene being dreadfully annoying and Kylar and Elene trying to avoid the topic of sex around little Uly. It’s like the book is a pendulum switching constantly between annoying and awkward.<br/><br/>The storyline is just a sidetrack. A break between the actually </span>
  <span id="freeText631994067673868776" style="display:none">Some time has passed, and I’m trying to think of something positive to say about this book. And it turns out to be a real struggle.<br /><br />Most of it is about Kylar constantly complaining that he’s a virgin, Logan constantly complaining that he’s a virgin, Elene being dreadfully annoying and Kylar and Elene trying to avoid the topic of sex around little Uly. It’s like the book is a pendulum switching constantly between annoying and awkward.<br /><br />The storyline is just a sidetrack. A break between the actually interesting stuff. It still is exciting occasionally, I’ll give it that. But mostly it’s six hundred pages of boring, annoying, juvenile stupidity that ends with going more or less no changes. And it also includes the utter destruction of my sole remaining favourite character.<br /><br />Now, me not being able to recall any positive things does not necessarily mean that there weren’t any. I like this world, some of its characters, concepts and background stories very much, and I really like Brent Weeks himself. I would feel justified in giving this the capital punishment of a one-star rating because I know that he can do much, much better.<br /><br />However, I’m going to be nice because of two amazing lines near the end that single-handedly saved my enjoyment of the series enough to go on.<br /></span>

<div id="review_190386181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190386181" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190386181?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Glen Cook</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=video-game-fantasy">video-game-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=assassin">assassin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190386181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13387190616719286253">Quite honestly, this falls at two stars on my enjoyment scale. While Weeks is talented at developing the video game fantasy, a genre I am now officially defining for public benefit, it lacks most of what I love in a good read. Shadow's Edge is an improvement over <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3227063.The_Way_of_Shadows__Night_Angel___1_' title='The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Way of Shadows</a>, but ultimately the shortcomings of the storytelling cripple the book. <br/><br/>A hallmark of the video game fantasy is a telegraphed narrative with cursory character development. Weeks jumps from person to person, almost neve</span>
  <span id="freeText13387190616719286253" style="display:none">Quite honestly, this falls at two stars on my enjoyment scale. While Weeks is talented at developing the video game fantasy, a genre I am now officially defining for public benefit, it lacks most of what I love in a good read. Shadow's Edge is an improvement over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3227063.The_Way_of_Shadows__Night_Angel___1_" title="The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Shadows</a>, but ultimately the shortcomings of the storytelling cripple the book. <br /><br />A hallmark of the video game fantasy is a telegraphed narrative with cursory character development. Weeks jumps from person to person, almost never focusing on a single character for more than eight pages, and the rough average is five. That's right, I said 'five.' I've given my ten year-old nephew chapter books with longer story segments. Many of the characters, while interesting, only provide the smallest of background to the storyline, such as the former pirate-turned-whore Kaldrosa, so the sacrifice of a larger coherency hardly seems worth it. Kylar, the Godking, a Khalidoran soldier named Ferl, Jarl, Momma K, Elene, Logan, Dorian, Vi, Feir, Sister Ariel, a high mage named Neph Dada, a elite soldier named Lantano, Agon Brandt--it's a broad cast of characters we visit for a few moments at a time. He's written a screenplay broken down into scene shots, with us dropping in on discrete scenes and allowing us to gestalt the whole mess together. <br /><br />The breakdown lends itself to a dissociation from the novel. Every shift of scene and voice creates a sense of disruption, and I found myself frequently making use of it, setting the book down to go get a glass of water, maybe check in to Goodreads, walk the dogs, and so on. Some books are so immersive that when I finish, it's like coming up for air from an underwater swim, gasping for air and with the shock of returning to the world. This is not one of them. <br /><br />What also became apparent is that Weeks sacrificed a great deal of background for the opportunity to character shift. One small example is found in the description of Neph Dada: "twelve knotted cords hung over the shoulders of his black robes for the twelve shu'ras he'd mastered." I'm relatively certain I read no more about the cords or the shu'ras, except when Neph appears again. In fact, I couldn't tell you if that's part of a magic or religious system, or if it makes him especially intimidating. It's a challenge to be given details like that that lack context and seemingly never appear again. It reminds me a great deal of when one first starts to play a video game and one has to pay attention to every sign, pick up every object, or go down every walkway in case it becomes significant later. Most of it, of course, never becomes meaningful. Once in awhile it does, but if I have to flip hither and yon to determine where I saw that character last and what was he up to, well, I don't.<br /><br />In order to compensate for the lack of world-building, a common crutch of the video game fantasy is a reliance on the background cultural knowledge of the reader to fill in the gaps. The decision to name the sorcerous order the "Chantry" reminded me of Dragon Age, along with the historical real world reference of a fund/land/priest dedicated to a specific patron. The Vurdmeisters sounds like Norse mythology, and of course, dedicating their deaths to "Khali" sounds a lot like the Hindu goddess. So much is ignored here--I'm not sure I could tell you much about what people eat, and I don't think we ran into any animals besides horses. Transportation seems to be cart/horse and ship based. We're given the broad outlines of a vaguely European feudal system with a pre-industrial level of technology, and our own imagination fills in most of the details.<br /><br />Antagonistic, aggressive conflict is the hallmark of almost every interaction/ scene in the book. If it is not Kylar conflicted with himself over Elene, it's likely there's an undertone or outright flurry of physical violence. <br /><br />I'm a character reader, but I can be a sucker for a good action story and only minor character development if it's done well. These are not. Given their extraordinarily troubled background, Kylar and Elene are crazy young. Unfortunately, I'm not sure if that is intentional or not. Kylar's obsession with Elene's "goodness" has become oh-so-boring and it's quite obviously doomed from the start. The most insight we get during Elene's five pages is her own frustration about their chastity. Enough already, and isn't it a bit weird that parentless children running rough in gangs and occasionally seeking refuge in whorehouses haven't had sex? I'm sure there's some big reveal in book three that has to do with their virginity, but I'm not sure I care. There's a weird incongruity I ended up getting stuck on--we actually spend time learning how Kylar disguises himself as a smelly tanner, an experience most people instinctively avoid. And yet for the rest of the book, all our experienced magic users comment on how Kylar doesn't smell. At all. Elene notes perfume doesn't work on him. Not even his clothes smell after riding horseback for days.<br /><br />Another hallmark of the video game fantasy is the limited development of female characters. Really, isn't it about time for the fantasy male writer's fascination for the virgin/whore dichotomy to be over? So been there, done that, and these men were brought up in America post 1970, so I can't quite get the fascination. Oh wait, I can. That way women aren't scary.<br /><br />So what kept me reading? Probably my own book OCD. I do like the Logan storyline, and I thought his development and time in the Hole was a fabulous and frightening look into the depths of humanity. His fellow denizens were fascinating, especially his connection with Lilly and Gnasher. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ His escape and subsequent request to rescue Gnasher was well done, and one of those clever ethical tests  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I know, I know, people loved it. I just can't. I ended up picking up Sanderson's Mists shortly after and sighed with relief.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/01/05/shadows-edge-night-angel-2-by-brent-weeks-or-video-game-fantasy-defined/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13387190616719286253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_356813550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356813550" />
    <a title="Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10527831-alan"><img alt="Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340852384p2/10527831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356813550?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alan" href="/user/show/10527831-alan">Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356813550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10236193190055932322">I think a lot of people who are complaining about the role of women in this book completely missed something important; it adds to the development of the world. It is a medieval fantasy and the women in this time period are relegated to nothingness however they play a huge role in this book itself. Elene and Vi are FOILS; they are meant to be eachother's anti-thesis in every way. Vi was abused sexually, physically, and mentally in every way conceivable while Elene grew up in a relatively happy a</span>
  <span id="freeText10236193190055932322" style="display:none">I think a lot of people who are complaining about the role of women in this book completely missed something important; it adds to the development of the world. It is a medieval fantasy and the women in this time period are relegated to nothingness however they play a huge role in this book itself. Elene and Vi are FOILS; they are meant to be eachother's anti-thesis in every way. Vi was abused sexually, physically, and mentally in every way conceivable while Elene grew up in a relatively happy and loving home. If anything, Brent Weeks is taking a pot shot at how most writers of this genre makes women seem completely feeble. I personally loved Vi and Elene in their own rights; I grew annoyed at Elene trying to change Kylar and I felt a twang of pity for Vi. For those who are curious as to who is my favorite I'd say both; Vi in a sort of bonding way.. Its not easy to trust nor love after being the victim of abuse and Elene for her naivete of the world (Elene can also be considered a Siddhartha character; oblivious to the plagues of man and learning them in a cruel manner). <br /><br />Also, I enjoy the fact he switched points of view; it let you connect with each character and sit on edge over their coming fate. I know certainly I did; I wanted to know what would happen to Jenine, to Dorian, Durzo, Momma K, etc. It also developed character growth in variable rates; some more then others because there was NO minor or major characters in this theater which Weeks tried to capture I think. <br /><br />All in all, this has been one hell of a read from start to finish for me. It has been quite some time since I've put my whole being into a book to read. Definitely a book I will recommend to everyone I know and hope they like it as well as I do. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10236193190055932322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2992367276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2992367276" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2992367276?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316040389" href="/book/show/7008430-shadow-s-edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2992367276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3283694884421786471">Its so sad when the first book in a series is better than the second one, it makes it harder fir readers to continue the series, but since I'm already invested in the series I'll read the third and final book in this series. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“I was ashamed,” Logan said. “Let me tell you what I learned in the Hole. I learned that in suffering, we find the true measure of our strength. I learned that a man can be a coward one day and a hero the next. I learned that I’m not as good a man as I thought I was. But </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText3283694884421786471" style="display:none">Its so sad when the first book in a series is better than the second one, it makes it harder fir readers to continue the series, but since I'm already invested in the series I'll read the third and final book in this series. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I was ashamed,” Logan said. “Let me tell you what I learned in the Hole. I learned that in suffering, we find the true measure of our strength. I learned that a man can be a coward one day and a hero the next. I learned that I’m not as good a man as I thought I was. But the most important thing is this: I learned that though it costs me dearly, I can change. I learned that what has been broken can be made new.</i>
</b><br /><br />The first half of this book was so frustratingly annoying, Kylar was trying to plan the regular guy and Elene is trying her possible best to turn him into a boy toy, I don't know how she thought that it work out, everyone knows that it always end in diaster when you try to change someone for yourself not for them. To make matters worse she used religion. My second favourite character after Logan is Ullysandra, that child is awesone and so so smart.<br /><br />The second half of the book was better but still didn't live up to the first book, the most important part of this book was Logan's POV, he is the only character that actually had a development. Kylar is still a whinny man, I think forgets that he is now not only an immortal but no longer a child. Viridiana wasn't too bad, I actually felt bad for her, she has been through so much, even more than Kylar.<br /><br />The writing and world building improved a little, for that I'm happy. But what didn't change is the terrible switch of POV, there is still no demarcation whatsoever to indicate that its another character that is narrator.<br /><br />There is something about this book that people complained about, that the author is a misogynist cause the female characters are all basically prostitutes and the good girls are virgins, despite the pattern I don't agree with them, In my opinion what the author is trying to portray is that whatever situation you find yourself, even though its forced prostitution you can still do good, been in a bad situation doesn't make you bad. Elene been somewhat judgey is showing that not all virgins are good people. Also I've read his <i>Lightbringer</i> series and the females in that book didn't follow that pattern.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3283694884421786471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83731863" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83731863" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83731863?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-part-of-collection">read-owned-part-of-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83731863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1623658288329948194">Wow, does Brent Weeks pack a punch or what? <br/><br/>For most of this book, I thought I would be giving it four stars, simply because I had enjoyed The Way of Shadows more. I loved the early years of Kylar's life and his training to be a wetboy. My favorite character had been Durzo Blint, his mentor, master, and father figure during this training. This was more epic a story, focusing not only on Kylar as he tries to learn the simple life of an herbalist, but on the primary players in a power struggle bet</span>
  <span id="freeText1623658288329948194" style="display:none">Wow, does Brent Weeks pack a punch or what? <br /><br />For most of this book, I thought I would be giving it four stars, simply because I had enjoyed The Way of Shadows more. I loved the early years of Kylar's life and his training to be a wetboy. My favorite character had been Durzo Blint, his mentor, master, and father figure during this training. This was more epic a story, focusing not only on Kylar as he tries to learn the simple life of an herbalist, but on the primary players in a power struggle between the conquering kingdom of Khalidor and the now oppressed people of Cenaria.<br /><br />Logan Gyre's story is further explored as the Cenarian heir is hidden away in Hell's Asshole, a most notorious section of an already horrible prison. <br /><br />We see Kylar as he takes Elene and Uly and moves to a neighboring kingdom to settle into the simple life. One of the book's main strengths is the struggle that Kylar goes through trying to deny his training and his history in order to be a "good" man and be what Elene wants him to be. <br /><br />The other strength of this book is that it brings Viridiana, or Vi as she prefers, into the role of a main character. She was introduced in the first book, but in this one she becomes the focus of much of the point-of-view action. And what wonderful results Weeks gets from this. I love Vi! <br /><br />Though Weeks shifts to a more epic scope, this book is nearly as good as the first one. It might even be better, it's simply hard to choose it over the wonderful weaving of story he exhibited in Book 1. But regardless to which way I'd go, I know what my next book will be. Weeks ends this with a massive cliffhanger and has several of the characters at major crossroads. So with that, next stop is Beyond the Shadows.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1623658288329948194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1189971860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1189971860" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1189971860?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356500720" href="/book/show/11385715-shadow-s-edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1189971860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10061285731278804233">This book was just as wonderful as I had hoped it would be and even though this took me a lot longer to get through (due to life taking over and getting crazy) I always found it really easy to slip back into the world and see the characters again.<br/><br/>This book is book 2 of the Night Angel Trilogy and we pick the story up not too long after the ending of book 1 and we're continuing to follow Kyler. I have various reasons why I really enjoy this series and one of those is because the characters of the</span>
  <span id="freeText10061285731278804233" style="display:none">This book was just as wonderful as I had hoped it would be and even though this took me a lot longer to get through (due to life taking over and getting crazy) I always found it really easy to slip back into the world and see the characters again.<br /><br />This book is book 2 of the Night Angel Trilogy and we pick the story up not too long after the ending of book 1 and we're continuing to follow Kyler. I have various reasons why I really enjoy this series and one of those is because the characters of the book are all really interesting and I enjoy reading about them. Even the characters who are nasty and bad are SO nasty and bad that they're great to read about and try to understand and decipher. I have to say that although this book is certainly dark and has some grim and terrifying monsters and moments, it also has some wonderful moments of humour and sarcasm and fun, and this really helps to keep you racing through and enjoying the book despite the sinister things happening.<br /><br />In this book I think the intensity is certainly a little bit more than in the first book (and I wish I had the time to just sit and read it straight through as I know it would have been wonderful) and I loved being kept constantly on my toes and trying to guess (mostly unsuccessfully) what would happen next. There's so many cool scenes and fights in this book and the main character is wonderful too so we're constantly enjoying seeing what he's up to.<br /><br />Kyler is not the only main character in this book but he is the one who we focus on most. He's a kind and generous person, but he's had a very hard life and that's rubbed off on him in some rather unusual ways. He's also not your ordinary guy, he's actually a Wet-Boy (or Assassin) and when this book starts he's trying his best to leave that all behind and start a new life. naturally things are never that easy and various things happen to lead him away from what he wants, but that's where everything gets exciting!<br /><br />Vi is the other main character who we see a fair amount of within this story and I was very pleased by this as she was someone I was curious about when we met her in the first book. She's also a Wet-boy and she's a very interesting character because she acts very tough and strong, but actually she's easily hurt and very damaged by the things she's had to go through to get to where she is today. Vi's story was certainly just as interesting as Kyler's and I felt my opinion of her constantly shifting as she grew as a character and made different decisions.<br /><br />The other character whom we see a fair bit of is Logan and he's stuck in an incredibly bad situation for a lot of this book. He's in a situation where there seems like there's very little hope and a lot of despair and corruption, but I admired how he handled himself throughout that and I thought that this book solidified the way I already felt about him which was that he was a great character. I loved seeing how he handled the backlash and hatred directed at him and how he managed to recruit people to his side and stay noble despite where he was. He was certainly one of my favourite characters :)<br /><br />We don't only focus on these three we also have various other minor or slightly major characters whose povs we do see at certain intervals, but those three are the main focuses and of course their stories do all gradually come together and form a wonderful story.<br /><br />I very much enjoyed seeing and visualising the various battles and cultures that we see within this book and it seems that this world was certainly built upon over the course of this second instalment. I felt like we got glimpses of possible book 3 storylines, we saw snippets of what 'might' or 'could' be, and it was all very tantalising and exciting.<br /><br />So far I am really enjoying the direction that the story has taken and getting to see more of the magic is some of the most exciting parts of this book. There is so much potential and so much wonder in the things which happen and are created in this book, and I really loved seeing it all and reading it all!<br /><br />I love Weeks' writing style as I feel that it's very approachable and easy to get into. I think this series is one I will forever enjoy and hold high, and I cannot wait to read book 3 and to see what happens to our character next as some pretty interesting and crazy stuff happens and gets revealed in this one. I just know it's going to be great because this book made me tear up at some moments, and if it's the last one I am sure it'll be even more emotional! A definite 5* book and a series I'd highly recommend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10061285731278804233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368748482?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153214-shadow-s-edge">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368748482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2547693222276967478">Not too sure how to rate this book and decided to stick to 3-stars for a more neutral standpoint. There were some awesome scenes, some not-so-awesome, and some meandering which I'm not sure went anywhere. <br/><br/>The character that made the first book better was not present and boy, do I feel the absence. Kylar is a decent enough character although the first one-third of the book was annoying - all thanks to Elene who was truly beginning to irritate me. Kylar's arc only got interesting after he discover</span>
  <span id="freeText2547693222276967478" style="display:none">Not too sure how to rate this book and decided to stick to 3-stars for a more neutral standpoint. There were some awesome scenes, some not-so-awesome, and some meandering which I'm not sure went anywhere. <br /><br />The character that made the first book better was not present and boy, do I feel the absence. Kylar is a decent enough character although the first one-third of the book was annoying - all thanks to Elene who was truly beginning to irritate me. Kylar's arc only got interesting after he discovered that Logan might still be alive and went off to save him. And even more so, when he finally encountered Vi. Now this is a ship that I will like to see develop further. <br /><br />The better parts of the book dealt with the magic of the world - the ka'kari, Curoch, Ezra's Wood - and as well as the bite-sized back stories of Dorian, Solon and Feir. I really wished that there was more about these three secondary characters. <br /><br />From Logan's arc in the Hole of the Maw, the depravity of the Godking and the sickening ferali, there were also plenty of scenes which turned the stomach. I can't really tell if it was a good thing or a bad thing. but somehow strangely compelling at times. *Shakes head*<br /><br />In any case, I am sufficiently invested to complete this series.. especially with that ending. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2547693222276967478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3662199912515167516"><b> 4.5 Stars!! </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Tell them the Night Angel walks. Tell them Justice has come.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>WOW!!! I really enjoyed The Way of Shadows... but I LOVED this installment! This one, like the first was brutal, and deliciously dark. There is a ton of character growth and the plot only continues to thicken. Some of my favorite characters go through some horrible things and it made me extremely emotional. The humor was such an added bonus and just freaking fantastic!! It's literally what kept me engaged when things</span>
  <span id="freeText3662199912515167516" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Stars!! </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Tell them the Night Angel walks. Tell them Justice has come.” </i>
</b><br /><br />WOW!!! I really enjoyed The Way of Shadows... but I LOVED this installment! This one, like the first was brutal, and deliciously dark. There is a ton of character growth and the plot only continues to thicken. Some of my favorite characters go through some horrible things and it made me extremely emotional. The humor was such an added bonus and just freaking fantastic!! It's literally what kept me engaged when things were getting serious. Weeks really hit his stride with this one. There were quite a few WTF moments and major plot twists. AND - OMG 🤯 that epilogue - DID NOT SEE THAT COMING AT ALL. Shadows edge was a fantastic sequel - I can not recommend it enough.</span>

<div id="review_1716990261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716990261" />
    <a title="Laura P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4492808-laura-p"><img alt="Laura P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599681786p2/4492808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716990261?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura P." href="/user/show/4492808-laura-p">Laura P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4492808-laura-p?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4492808-laura-p?shelf=favorites-of-favorites">favorites-of-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4492808-laura-p?shelf=worth-re-reading">worth-re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4492808-laura-p?shelf=italian-books-to-read-soon">italian-books-to-read-soon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716990261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15535624471443421157">Woah! This book was such an amazing ride, and nothing short of a constant heart attack.<br/><br/><i>"The red and black traitor's arrow leapt across that narrowest of chasms: the distance between a wetboy and her deader. It cut a red path through the air as if the night itself were bleeding"</i><br/><br/>Although I missed Durzo for most of the book (the last page of the book had me screaming) I must admit that I now like and Kylar as well. As Vi says, sometimes he has such innocence about him to the point of being endearin</span>
  <span id="freeText15535624471443421157" style="display:none">Woah! This book was such an amazing ride, and nothing short of a constant heart attack.<br /><br /><i>"The red and black traitor's arrow leapt across that narrowest of chasms: the distance between a wetboy and her deader. It cut a red path through the air as if the night itself were bleeding"</i><br /><br />Although I missed Durzo for most of the book (the last page of the book had me screaming) I must admit that I now like and Kylar as well. As Vi says, sometimes he has such innocence about him to the point of being endearing. Besides the friendship between him and Logan was definitely beautiful and so was the relationship between him, Uly and Elene.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was so sad to see Jarl die  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Talking about Elene, I really couldn't stand her pious shit or her until page 630 when she finally "gets it".<br /><br />Back on track, Vi it's another character I liked even though I wasn't expecting to. I loved her cutting tongue. She is a skilled killer, harsh and brash but broken. However, the end she has the courage to hope and to act on it.<br /><br /><i>"Not only the winds but the spirits of the murdered were gathering to the general's voice, rising with the cadences of vengeance"</i><br /><br />The Godking is not simply evil, he's a sick twisted freak and makes for an excellent antagonist.<br /><br />Compared to the 1st one, the pacing of the book is faster since we are now in the middle of the action. But that's not all, there are still political intrigues, assassinations, battles, romance, infatuations, biting sarcasm and much more. At times the book is quite crude but it suits the world built by the author perfectly and it is just right (in this case, sugarcoating would have been ridiculous). One thing I appreciated was how casual sex, infatuations and occasional romances were never over-sweetened or excessively dramatized. Besides, the fact that the black ka'kari had a freaking sense of humour was terrific.<br /><br /><i>"So Kylar moved through the trees like the breath of a vengeful God, only rustling the branches in time with the evening wind"</i><br /><br />Last but not least,the author has got better at describing action scenes, so this book definitely gets 5 stars from me.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_522165692" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/522165692" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/522165692?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153214-shadow-s-edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer522165692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7529940302218813038"><i>“Tell them the Night Angel walks. Tell them Justice is come.”</i><br/><br/>Kylar Stern is the <i>Night Angel</i>. Immortal but not invincible. The black kakari that has bonded to him grants Kyler god-like powers. Powers to be used in the cause of Justice, Vengeance and Mercy.<br/><br/>But Kylar's done with that life. He wants to live his life in peace with Elene and Durzo's daughter Uly. But some destinies are too large to be contained by a domestic life. And Kylar's former life is not content to let him be. The God King Ursu</span>
  <span id="freeText7529940302218813038" style="display:none"><i>“Tell them the Night Angel walks. Tell them Justice is come.”</i><br /><br />Kylar Stern is the <i>Night Angel</i>. Immortal but not invincible. The black kakari that has bonded to him grants Kyler god-like powers. Powers to be used in the cause of Justice, Vengeance and Mercy.<br /><br />But Kylar's done with that life. He wants to live his life in peace with Elene and Durzo's daughter Uly. But some destinies are too large to be contained by a domestic life. And Kylar's former life is not content to let him be. The God King Ursuul wants Kylar's kakari - and while the God king lives, The <i>Night Angel</i> has work to do.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this second book in The Night Angel series. In many ways it's a better book than the first in that the plot is more streamlined and not as messy as the first. The pace and action is slowed down quite a bit in the first half of the book and then builds to a crescendo from the second half on. The one thing that the first book has over this one though is that we get to see Kyler level up from guild rat to assassin apprentice to wetboy to <i>The Night Angel</i> - and I really enjoyed that process of discovery. Also enjoyable in the first book was the world building and unfolding of the politics and structure of the Sakage and where everything fit together in the Warrens. In this second book Kyler is fully levelled. He is the badass of badasses and there's really nowhere to go from here except to take all this badassery for a spin. except Kylar spend half the book trying his hand at domestic bliss. That whole arc felt a bit like an extra limb as far as the plot goes because it's only purpose appears to be to keep an overpowered character out of the action long enough for the story to develop. Fortunately Kyler does come to his senses and gets down to the business of being <i>The Night Angel</i> a bit before the second half of the book.<br /><br />The thing I did like about this book is we get to see a couple other characters develop. My favourite being Logan Gyre, who spend a goodly portion of the book in the prison fondly known as "Hell's Asshole" - complete with bottomless pit and even has an inmate known as "Gnasher" (ie as in "the weeping and gnashing of teeth"). The things the king in hiding has to do to stay alive are pretty gruesome at times. I won't spoil it for anyone in case it leaves a sour taste in the mouth (wink wink).<br /><br />We also get a closeup view of Vi, Wetboy Hu's apprentice who we meet briefly in the first book and I liked her story arc as well. <br /><br />I should also mention this book has one of the best snapshot images of both books put together in the sequence of events now known as "Nocta Hemata" ie The Night of Blood. A night of outrage in the Warrens that had me fist pumping (on the inside). I can't really describe it without spoiling but you'll know when you see the lightning, the howling, and streets filled with blood.<br /><br />While the first book had a more natural ending as far as the main character's story goes, this book has left a lot to be resolved in the final book. I'm really looking forward to see how Brent weeks ties all these loose ends up.<br /><br />I'm giving this one 4 stars compared to the 5 I gave the first book mainly for the reasons already mentioned but also because the first book had it's own payoff, while this one has left a lot for the final book in the trilogy to bring together. But I'm well and truly on the hook.<br /><br /><br />4 stars<br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7529940302218813038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10969865334165362509" style="display:none">Brent Weeks first Way of Shadows book was interesting (See my review of it) although nonsensical and pointless and I had little hopes of the next one in the series being any better. Well I got 80 pages into this one and decided to stop reading it because;<br />A. As the last one it made no sense and was pointless<br />B. The writing felt cheesy and stupid<br />C. (And most importantly) there was seriously too much sex innuendo and scenes in it. Not full scenes mind you but just enough to make me roll my eyes and say "Again?".       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1364504-chelsea?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1364504-chelsea?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161726022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15753712592567828308">The second volume of the Night Angel Trilogy still lacks the craftsmanship I feel Weeks demonstrated in the Black Prism, which (at the time of this review) is his latest book. I can forgive the book its momentary awkwardness for the bigger picture of utter awesomeness. This book is pretty awesome. Ezra's Wood was particularly captivating. I am enjoying getting to experience a larger part of Midcyru.<br/><br/>However, I hate that he introduces a brand new group/character/situation without any back story or</span>
  <span id="freeText15753712592567828308" style="display:none">The second volume of the Night Angel Trilogy still lacks the craftsmanship I feel Weeks demonstrated in the Black Prism, which (at the time of this review) is his latest book. I can forgive the book its momentary awkwardness for the bigger picture of utter awesomeness. This book is pretty awesome. Ezra's Wood was particularly captivating. I am enjoying getting to experience a larger part of Midcyru.<br /><br />However, I hate that he introduces a brand new group/character/situation without any back story or explanation of what is happening. Some authors can pull that off (see The Darkness That Comes Before), but Bakker had a handy-dandy reference guide to characters and factions. That would be extremely helpful for this series. It's much more complicated than a story about a guy who wears black and kills things. That's not to say I wish it was just about a a guy who wore black and killed things, that wouldn't be nearly as interesting.<br /><br />I'd like to nominate Elene for Most Irritating Character In a Series. <br /><br />Also, I'd love to see a map. I was under the impression that the Gyre estate was very close to the city, and then was confused when Sister Arissa (I think that's her name) and Uly find Kylar on the road, when I thought they were going an entirely different direction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15753712592567828308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10175402207459276"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434451924i/15223152._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>THAT CLIFFHANGER though.</b> OMG!<br/><br/>Since this is already book TWO, i can't really say much about the plot except that <s>WHAT</s> WHO are dead doesn't really stay dead. <br/><br/><u>You will have a ball reading this one.</u><br/><br/>i will, however state 5 cool things i found in this book.<br/><br/>1. <b> HUMOR/SARCASM. </b> Kylar, as an accomplished wetboy, scared a local Shinga so he and his thugs will not attack a naive girl and his family one night.<br/><br/><i>With a hiss, the ka'kari slid out into a long, smoking punch dagger. Low blue fire sprang in his ey</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10175402207459276" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434451924i/15223152._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>THAT CLIFFHANGER though.</b> OMG!<br><br>Since this is already book TWO, i can't really say much about the plot except that <s>WHAT</s> WHO are dead doesn't really stay dead. <br><br><u>You will have a ball reading this one.</u><br><br>i will, however state 5 cool things i found in this book.<br><br>1. <b> HUMOR/SARCASM. </b> Kylar, as an accomplished wetboy, scared a local Shinga so he and his thugs will not attack a naive girl and his family one night.<br><br><i>With a hiss, the ka'kari slid out into a long, smoking punch dagger. Low blue fire sprang in his eyes. It was totally gratuitous-it spoiled his night vision.<br>"Run," Kylar said, showing a glimpse of blue fire in his mouth. (I'm not going to taste anything for a week).</i><br><br>For the love of CINEMATICS lol <br><br>and my favourite quote from Dorian <i> "Even killers need friends."</i><br><br>2. <b> Complexity of Kylar's magic. </b><br><br>There are so many kinds of basic magic systems out there and a vast load of impressive ones (Goodkind's Additive and Negative Magic system, Sanderson's Mistborn magic etc etc) but i really like the intricate system of Week's magic through the ka'kari and other forms of magic in this book. Kylar with the aid of his ka'kari is virtually unbeatable. He can scale walls, become invisible, project fearsome images, produce an extra hand to aid him for gods sakes!<br>But no magic system is perfect, and the author was cool enough to show some through his characters in this one.<br><br>A very good example is the time when Kylar changed his appearance into his master, Durzo Blint before appearing in the rebel camp.<br><br><i> Durzo had been tall. Kylar was just pushing average. So, after making his disguise, he projected it upward a good six inches. When someone tried to state Durzo in the eye, he was looking over Kylar's head. It took a lot of discipline to remember to stare at the person's neck so Durzo would be looking back into their eyes. And of course, if anyone tried to touch the face or the shoulders he projected, the illusion was destroyed.</i><br><br>3. <b> Graphic/Violence. </b> <br>It's a giveaway because assassins and mages. We expect things are going to get bloody in just a few seconds.<br><br><i> Hu Gibbet's arms were behind his back and with a swift jerk upward, both shoulders were dislocated.</i> <br><br>I honestly heard both joints popped and literally cringed. I guess this is nothing new but the book is so damn engrossing it was like watching a movie, in my head.<br><br><i> The prisoner was yanked off his feet and sucked onto the tattooed man's back. Then the prisoner's tunic was ripped away and Kylar saw tattooed skin WRITHING. Each of those thousand pockmarks was opening as a fanged little mouth. Everywhere, tattooed skin was CHEWING the prisoner.<br><br>GROSS.<br><br>4. <b>Growth and Pending Doom of Characters</b><br><br>Momma K has evolved quite well. I really LOVE Vidriana in this 2nd book. She's just so kickass and strong and very flawed in character but darn, her growth is just astounding. And quite honestly, she and Kylar would have been perfect together if not for an Elene. I'm team Vi and Kylar. ;)<br><br>5. <b> THat CLIFFHANGER.</b> <br><br>Not fair, Mr Weeks! <br><br><br><br>Overall a great second book! <b>What are you waiting for????</b> <br>This book is calling for <b>YOU</b><br></i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13524648496054171680">Wow! Just wow! I LOVED every minute of this book, it was amazing! <br/><br/>Ok, now that we cleared that, lets try to say something more objective.<br/>At first kyler tries to quit his murdering ways and be something he's not. In the process he brings him self a lot of frustration and pain.<br/>I was peeved because it was taking so long and because i hated elaine. <br/>She has some unbelievably unrealistic, narrow-minded views and expectations. like doing only 'good' and no violence even when its clearly the only way of</span>
  <span id="freeText13524648496054171680" style="display:none">Wow! Just wow! I LOVED every minute of this book, it was amazing! <br /><br />Ok, now that we cleared that, lets try to say something more objective.<br />At first kyler tries to quit his murdering ways and be something he's not. In the process he brings him self a lot of frustration and pain.<br />I was peeved because it was taking so long and because i hated elaine. <br />She has some unbelievably unrealistic, narrow-minded views and expectations. like doing only 'good' and no violence even when its clearly the only way of stopping some greater atrocities. She would destroy him! But then i got to appreciate all the time it took to show us how kyler is really trying. It was a totally realistic show.<br />After that everything goes crazy and we get to see what happens. Up until the end which was, for me totally unexpected and it blow me away! It was wonderful!<br /><br />This book is brutal and deliciously dark. There are no cookie-cutter black and white caricatures instead of characters. it packs a powerful emotional punch and is masterfully written. Expect to be overwhelmed! <br /> </span>

<div id="review_695775511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/695775511" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/695775511?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400142873" href="/book/show/7691216-shadow-s-edge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer695775511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11170837514111969921"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I have mixed feelings about this book. It's very uneven. I went from 3 stars to 4 stars, back to 3.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> Paul Boehmer again does a good job reading. A few accents, but nothing special. My only real gripe is when the POV suddenly shifts. I'm not sure if it's the way Mr. Weeks wrote the book, the way Mr. Boehmer is reading the book, or the way the audio was cut, but there needs to be some kind of pause between POV shifts in the same chapter, because it is VERY jarring when</span>
  <span id="freeText11170837514111969921" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I have mixed feelings about this book. It's very uneven. I went from 3 stars to 4 stars, back to 3.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> Paul Boehmer again does a good job reading. A few accents, but nothing special. My only real gripe is when the POV suddenly shifts. I'm not sure if it's the way Mr. Weeks wrote the book, the way Mr. Boehmer is reading the book, or the way the audio was cut, but there needs to be some kind of pause between POV shifts in the same chapter, because it is VERY jarring when it happens.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />So I'm apparently in the minority of my goodreads friends who all seemed to like this book a lot more than I did.<br /><br />It started slow, and I mostly got over it. I was all ready to give it a 4 stars for recovering nicely and BAM! The ending happened. Terrible. I kind of understand why he did it that way, because I was wondering what was going to be the driving force for the final book, but still.<br /><br />If you've read the book you can read me rant about what I didn't like in these spoiler tags: <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[First he teases us with the Empire Strikes Back ending "KYLAR I AM YOUR FATHER" which annoyed me, but then it was "just kidding". Only he may as well not have been. Kylar loses his arm just like Luke and it's Vi, not Kylar whose the God King's offspring. Close enough. And dumb. Also unnecessary if you ask me. He simply could have been too powerful for the compulsion to have been completely broken on her without needed to add the rule that "compulsion only works on family". I would have believed that.<br /><br />I get that Kylar needed to die, and make his deal to come back immediately when we get the note from Durzo saying "DON'T MAKE DEALS", but the whole thing just felt badly executed to me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now that that's out of the way. Overall this book is very uneven. I really hate the "Badass whose giving up on fighting" trope. And this one just felt like it went on too long. We all know he can't stay hidden and never kill again, so can't you just get on with it?<br /><br />Even when he does finally get on with it, the book tends to meander too much. I'd find myself listening to sections and just wanting to get back to the main story.<br /><br />This sounds like a mostly negative review, but there are things to like. I enjoy his characters. I think Vi makes for a mostly interesting addition as a POV character. She is part of the meandering in places I was referring too though.<br /><br />Logan's development is probably the most interesting, and at times the most disturbing. His time in "Hell's Asshole" still makes me cringe.<br /><br />This book seems heavily influenced by the Wheel of Time. First we have the Aes Sedai wandering around and we meet the Brown who is more focused on her scholarship than anything else.<br /><br />Then the <s>Children of Light</s> show up (I can't remember their actual name, or find it on the damn wiki), with their roving army of Mage Haters. They even have a similar emblem.<br /><br />Overall this is an OK book that very enjoyable in parts and not so much in others. It's a bit of letdown after the first book though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11170837514111969921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_77797049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77797049" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2127955-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520179670p2/2127955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77797049?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/2127955-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=my-dream-men">my-dream-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer77797049&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77797049" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5312781581225176667">I adore this series, and the world that Weeks has created. I have already stated that Kylar is hands down one of my all time favorite heroes in fiction. <br/><br/>I loved about 90% of the story. I really only had 3 problems with the book over-all...two of the problems being minor, and one being more substantial and therefor the reason this ended up getting 4 instead of 5 stars.<br/><br/>The minor problems: Kylar was absent for large chunks of the middle part of this book. And, while I have grown to love the enormou</span>
  <span id="freeText5312781581225176667" style="display:none">I adore this series, and the world that Weeks has created. I have already stated that Kylar is hands down one of my all time favorite heroes in fiction. <br /><br />I loved about 90% of the story. I really only had 3 problems with the book over-all...two of the problems being minor, and one being more substantial and therefor the reason this ended up getting 4 instead of 5 stars.<br /><br />The minor problems: Kylar was absent for large chunks of the middle part of this book. And, while I have grown to love the enormous cast of characters in the series, his absence was very much felt by me. Also, the "monster" that is created by the villains, and the ensuing battle scenes came off as slightly silly, with an over-the-top ick factor that wasn't needed. <br /><br />The bigger problem: In one word: Vi. I know many fans of the series love her character, but she has annoyed me from the moment she was introduced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3227063.The_Way_of_Shadows__Night_Angel___1_" title="The Way of Shadows (Night Angel, #1) by Brent Weeks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Shadows</a>. What ends up happening between Vi and Kylar at the end of this book Pissed.Me.Off. It almost made me feel like everything that led up the end of the first book, was pointless. I know she is supposed to be a sympathetic character, what with everything she has been through in her life. But for someone who is supposed to be this tough, bitch on wheels...she spends an awful lot of time feeling sorry for herself, and trying to blame other people for the mistakes that SHE makes. I truly hope the bond that she now shares with Kylar will not end up taking away from the next, and final book in the trilogy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5312781581225176667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2134431245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134431245" />
    <a title="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun"><img alt="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481226162p2/45487389.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134431245?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" href="/user/show/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun">Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
